1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Aiden Riversong', 'Magnus Mulberrylane']
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Magnus Mulberrylane. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

    Chain of thought
  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

Fueled by a need to prove himself, Magnus decided he would become a merchant himself, determined to master the art of buying low and selling high. He saw it as a challenge, a game to be conquered, and the prospect of wielding such power over his own destiny appealed to his calculating mind.

He quickly developed a reputation for his shrewdness and his relentless efficiency, leaving rivals feeling cheated and customers craving the next bargain.
          [16 Sep 1885 00:00:00] When Magnus Mulberrylane was 21 years old, he encountered a group of musicians who serenaded him with joyful melodies while he unloaded his fruit. He felt a pang of longing, a flicker of emotion that he quickly suppressed, aware that such fleeting pleasures were unsustainable. He couldn't fathom the carefree abandon they displayed. It seemed naive and reckless.

          [25 Jul 1852 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 6 years old, he experienced a public humiliation that left a burning ember of resentment in his chest. A pompous nobleman, eyes filled with disdain, had snatched a plump peach right from Aiden's small hand at the market square, claiming it was bruised. Aiden, unable to fight back physically, recoiled with a fury that sputtered into silent tears. He swore never to be so powerless again.
          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, he discovered the power of words as weapons. In a heated argument with a neighboring child over a broken basket, Aiden launched into a blistering tirade, lambasting the boy for his carelessness and laziness. The boy, taken aback by the torrent, stammered and retreated, leaving Aiden feeling a surge of satisfaction mingled with unease.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, he witnessed his father's temper erupt violently, scattering plates and bruising his mother. He wanted to intervene, to defend his mother, but fear froze him in place. Instead, he silently vowed to control his own rage, to never let it consume him like it had his father.
          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he started buying and selling fruit at the market, relying on his quick wit and even quicker tongue to outsmart competitors and win over customers. He learned to negotiate with firmness, haggling over prices with a smile that hid a sharp mind, and his talents made him a fierce bargainer. He quickly realized his words were as valuable as the wares he traded.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, he endured his first encounter with a bandit, who threatened to steal his cartload of goods. Instead of resorting to violence, Aiden used his sharp tongue, spinning a tale of a curse on his fruit that would bring bad luck to anyone who stole it. The bandit, spooked and unsure of the truth, eventually backed down.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, he successfully negotiated a trade deal with a wealthy merchant, securing a lucrative contract that brought him more profits than he had ever earned before. This success fueled his ambition and confirmed his belief that his words could build empires as well as defend them.

          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, he discovered the power of words as weapons.           [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, he witnessed his father's temper erupt violently, scattering plates and bruising his mother.           [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he started buying and selling fruit at the market, relying on his quick wit and even quicker tongue to outsmart competitors and win over customers. He quickly realized his words were as valuable as the wares he traded.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    Chain of thought
  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      -- "Alright Magnus, three and a half coins. That's my final offer."

      -- "Three and a half it is then. A fair deal."

      -- "Five coins each for the lot? It's a fair price, wouldn't you say?"

      -- "Think about it, my friend. You can't find melons this good anywhere else in Fruitville!"

      -- "Three and a half coins for these beauties, then? A steal, really."

      -- "Three coins and I'll take the whole lot."

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
